                                                                              "message":  "No, that\u0027s not an accurate interpretation. The referenced point about asymmetric conflicts rarely resolving without significant external intervention does not equate to \"complete annihilation\" of the weaker party (in this case, Palestinians) as the inevitable alternative. Instead, it highlights how power imbalances often lead to prolonged stalemates, cycles of violence and negotiation, or entrenched dominance by the stronger side (Israel), where the conflict simmers without a mutually agreed peace. This can result in ongoing occupation, displacement, or fragmentation of the weaker side\u0027s capabilities, but not necessarily total destruction—historical patterns in similar conflicts show varied outcomes like indefinite status quo, gradual erosion of territory or autonomy, or even eventual withdrawal by the stronger power under internal or other pressures.\n\nFor context, no exact 2021 study in the *Journal of Conflict Resolution* directly matches the description provided, but related research on asymmetric conflicts (including Israel-Palestine) supports the broader idea. A 2009 analysis in the *Journal of Conflict Studies* on the Israeli-Palestinian dynamics describes the conflict as structurally asymmetric, with Israel leveraging military, legal, and political superiority to maintain control through strategies like settlement expansion and dividing Palestinian factions (e.g., between Gaza and the West Bank). Without external pressure (e.g., from the U.S. or international bodies), it argues the conflict tends to cycle between confrontation and failed negotiations, favoring Israel\u0027s status quo rather than leading to annihilation.\u003cgrok:render card_id=\"dca4c5\" card_type=\"citation_card\" type=\"render_inline_citation\"\u003e\n\u003cargument extermination.\u003cgrok:render card_id=\"335266\" card_type=\"citation_card\" type=\"render_inline_citation\"\u003e\n\u003cargument                                                                                                       "snippet":  "Journal of Conflict Studies 33 The Dynamics of Asymmetric Conflicts: The Israeli-Palestinian Case by Giorgio Gallo and Arturo Marzano ABSTRACT Asymmetry is considered one of the most relevant features in today’s conflicts. In this article we address one particular type of asymmetry — structural asymmetry. After introducing the main characteristics and different phases of these types of conflicts, i.e., conscientization, confrontation, negotiation, and sustainable peace, we address the specificity of the Israeli-Palestinian case presented here as a typical case of a structurally asymmetric conflict. The aim is to explain why, despite the many negotiation phases this conflict has been through, none has ever led to a sustainable peace.                                                                                                                                                                                            "snippet":  "Journal of Conflict Studies 33 The Dynamics of Asymmetric Conflicts: The Israeli-Palestinian Case by Giorgio Gallo and Arturo Marzano ABSTRACT Asymmetry is considered one of the most relevant features in today’s conflicts. In this article we address one particular type of asymmetry — structural asymmetry. After introducing the main characteristics and different phases of these types of conflicts, i.e., conscientization, confrontation, negotiation, and sustainable peace, we address the specificity of the Israeli-Palestinian case presented here as a typical case of a structurally asymmetric conflict. The aim is to explain why, despite the many negotiation phases this conflict has been through, none has ever led to a sustainable peace. On the contrary, each negotiation has brought on yet another confrontation phase, in a never-ending series of loops. The strong imbalance between the two sides and the scarce reciprocal conflict awareness represent the two main reasons for explaining this pattern. INTRODUCTION Wit",
